        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3197455859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10681962456629302049">4.25/5. Well this is a very unique slow-burn love story between two lonely and socially ostracised people, who agreed to a marriage of convenience out of desperation. She's a struggling widowed mother of two young ones and another in the oven. He is a newly released convicted murderer who answers her unconventional advertisement for a helper/husband to assist with the many physical tasks required to run her farm. <br/><br/>Ejected from yet another job due to his criminal past, Will is just grateful for fo</span>
  <span id="freeText10681962456629302049" style="display:none">4.25/5. Well this is a very unique slow-burn love story between two lonely and socially ostracised people, who agreed to a marriage of convenience out of desperation. She's a struggling widowed mother of two young ones and another in the oven. He is a newly released convicted murderer who answers her unconventional advertisement for a helper/husband to assist with the many physical tasks required to run her farm. <br /><br />Ejected from yet another job due to his criminal past, Will is just grateful for food to fill his gnawing belly and not to be looked at with distrust by another human being. Used to back-breaking hard work, he is more than willing and able to take on any task required for him to stay employed at this grossly neglected farm. If marriage is part of the deal, he'll take that too because it offers greater permanency. <br /><br /><i>She was almost as sorry-looking as her place, and pregnant to boot. He needed a dry bed, but preferably not one with her in it.</i> <br /><br />Eleanor grew up in an oppressive and abusive household, initially forbidden to interact with the outside world, and then when she was finally allowed this interaction through compulsory school attendance, she discovered this world to be unkind and judgemental - much like home. Only her husband had ever shown her goodness and affection and with him gone, her only link to society had disappeared with him. But being practical, she knows with her baby due within months that she and the kids will need the help of an outsider. <br /><br />Two people who grew up devoid of love and tenderness in their lives now bound together out of their common need for survival. Gradually, trust and affection bloom between them and both grow in confidence as individuals and in their interactions with others.<br /><br /><i><br />And at long, long last the loneliness of Will Parker’s life stopped hurting. He thought her name over and over—Elly... Elly—a benediction, as the kiss deepened, firmer, fuller, but still with a certain reserve—two people schooled to reject the possibility of miracles now forced to change their beliefs.<br /><br /><br />The sting hit his eyelids and he hung his head because nobody had prepared him for this, nobody had said, When it happens you’ll be resurrected. All that you were you will not be. All that you weren’t, you are.</i><br /><br /><br />Lovely story with sweet and vulnerable protagonists you just want to hug and protect. Their loneliness, their distrust in mankind, their raw needs to be loved, to be cared for, to be trusted by another - all depicted so well by the author. The setting, America just before and during WWII, is fascinating in its details of how life changed for the everyday American. I've read many WWII books, mostly from a European perspective, but never read about the impact on US soil. Will's interactions and growing fondness for Elly's boys are endearing. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10681962456629302049" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14068513928708900357"><b>4.5-stars</b> These characters make my heart swell.<br/><br/>I heard about Morning Glory a long while ago. Well, I am so glad I have finally read it! It is an incredible love story between two ordinary people Will and Elly. Will is an ex-convict and a drifter. Their journey begins with Will answering Elly’s ad. It is one of those romance books that go for simplicity and reality without ridiculous suspense and nonsense twist. I like Will’s sincerity and Elly’s generous spirit. Both LCs are damaged, but there a</span>
  <span id="freeText14068513928708900357" style="display:none"><b>4.5-stars</b> These characters make my heart swell.<br /><br />I heard about Morning Glory a long while ago. Well, I am so glad I have finally read it! It is an incredible love story between two ordinary people Will and Elly. Will is an ex-convict and a drifter. Their journey begins with Will answering Elly’s ad. It is one of those romance books that go for simplicity and reality without ridiculous suspense and nonsense twist. I like Will’s sincerity and Elly’s generous spirit. Both LCs are damaged, but there are no depressing tones in their voices. In the end, I am so damn proud of both characters. <br /><br />What to expect:<br />Strong heroine<br />No insta-love. No melodrama<br />Very likable LCs<br />Not a light fluffy/smut read<br />Heartwarming/human emotions<br />Great characters development and growth<br />World War II<br />Veterans<br />Childbirth<br />Slow pace ( It didn't bother me much. )<br />Something about bee and eagle: *swoon*<br /><i>“Did you know the workers practice something called flower fidelity? It means each bee gathers nectar and pollen from only one species of flower.”</i><br /><i>“Bald eagle mated for life?!?!”</i> <br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1065677126" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11296548055387446085">My favourite part about this novel was how slowly things developed. Some readers may not enjoy this and might prefer a more fast-paced novel, but I loved watching as their relationship developed and how mutual need for both turned to companionship and then love. I particularly enjoyed watching as they overcame their insecurities and misgivings. The book is told from more than one POV and during scenes--particularly ones that hold a lot of emotional weight--we see both the inner thoughts of Elly </span>
  <span id="freeText11296548055387446085" style="display:none">My favourite part about this novel was how slowly things developed. Some readers may not enjoy this and might prefer a more fast-paced novel, but I loved watching as their relationship developed and how mutual need for both turned to companionship and then love. I particularly enjoyed watching as they overcame their insecurities and misgivings. The book is told from more than one POV and during scenes--particularly ones that hold a lot of emotional weight--we see both the inner thoughts of Elly and Will and it's nice that when their relationship is put through the paces (quite a few times), the reader sees both Will and Elly's inner-thoughts and initial reactions. I felt their initial trepidation and self-doubt was very realistic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11296548055387446085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_18575388" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18575388" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/184500-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343560087p2/184500.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/184500-jennifer?shelf=romance">romance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18575388" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12228921072737599946">It's rare that an author can pull off having a hero who killed a whore in a brothel before the book and still have the reader like and forgive him, but Spencer did it. This was just wonderful. Both protagonists had so many insecurities and Spencer played them perfectly--they were real without overwhelming the plot and overcome realistically. This was lovely.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('R3Y+x+pfL6EVY6zkETbs+vrt2ydpR+P9vLmnXWYMOlEeCPcwTfvTdYGZ4thnkrUs+Ox3/c3t9vM2GP7QT9TCVA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OUGtaB5iGX6YH/YJj6jCCJA0nCVgIuxQ0VMRA3a7kqdgP2SfucblqgzluDX5DJvekjUw/8SI+V5b8kiOX2Nqog==')})
  }

They blame those lapses for the disgraceful fact that she is a spinster at 28.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/33987.LaVyrle_Spencer">About LaVyrle Spencer</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/33987.LaVyrle_Spencer"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_111x148-8060b12280b2aec7543bafb574ee8422.png);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11841809963390998931">LaVyrle Spencer is an American best-selling author of contemporary and historical romance novels. She has successfully published a number of books, with several of them made into movies. Twelve of her books have been New York Times bestsellers, and Spencer was inducted into the Romance Writers of America Hall of Fame in 1988. <br/><br/>Spencer is known for creating realistic characters and stories that focu</span>
  <span id="freeText11841809963390998931" style="display:none">LaVyrle Spencer is an American best-selling author of contemporary and historical romance novels. She has successfully published a number of books, with several of them made into movies. Twelve of her books have been New York Times bestsellers, and Spencer was inducted into the Romance Writers of America Hall of Fame in 1988. <br /><br />Spencer is known for creating realistic characters and stories that focus on families rather than only the relationship between a man and woman. These "ordinary" men and women are warm and vulnerable and are always portrayed sympathetically.[1] Her heroines tend to be a mix of fire and warmth, strength, savvy and soft–heartedness who must overcome some sort of adversity, such as pregnancy, divorce, a lengthy separation, the loss of a loved one, and then undergo a catharsis. The stories center on themes of abiding love, family ties and strength in difficult times.<br /><br />In the 1980s and 1990s Spencer wrote 12 New York Times Bestsellers. Her books have been sold to book clubs worldwide, and have been published around the world. Condensed versions of many of her novels have appeared in Reader's Digest and Good Housekeeping.<br /><br />She retired from writing in 1997.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11841809963390998931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
